The A320 is a low wing airliner with twin underwing turbofans\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Role\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_airliner" class="mw-redirect" title="Narrow-body February 1987\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Introduction\n</th>\n<td>18 April 1988 with <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a><sup id="cite_ref-Flight3sep1988_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight3sep1988-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Status\n</th>\n<td>In service\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Primary&#160;users\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a><sup id="cite_ref-aamerger_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aamerger-4">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup><br /><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Produced\n</th>\n<td>1986\xe2\x80\x93present\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Number built</span>\n</th>\n<td>9,798 as of 31&#160;March&#160;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n\n<tr>\n<th>Variants\n</th>\n<td><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A318" title="Airbus A318">Airbus A318</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a></li></ul></div>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th><span class="nowrap">Developed into</span>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo_family" title="Airbus A320neo family">Airbus A320neo family</a>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Airbus A320 family</b> are <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrow-body airliners</a> designed and produced by <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>.\nThe A320 was launched in March 1984, <a href="/wiki/Maiden_flight" title="Maiden flight">first flew</a> on 22 February 1987, and was introduced in April 1988 by <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>.\nThe first member of the family was followed by the longer A321 (first delivered in January 1994), the shorter A319 (April 1996), and the even shorter A318 (July 2003).\nFinal assembly takes place in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> in France; <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a> in Germany; <a href="/wiki/Tianjin" title="Tianjin">Tianjin</a> in China since 2009; and in <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a> in the United States since April 2016.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Twinjet" title="Twinjet">twinjet</a> has a six-abreast cross-section and is powered by either <a href="/wiki/CFM56" class="mw-redirect" title="CFM56">CFM56</a> or <a href="/wiki/IAE_V2500" title="IAE V2500">IAE V2500</a> turbofans, except the CFM56/<a href="/wiki/PW6000" class="mw-redirect" title="PW6000">PW6000</a> powered A318.\nThe family pioneered the use of digital <a href="/wiki/Fly-by-wire" title="Fly-by-wire">fly-by-wire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Side-stick" title="Side-stick">side-stick</a> flight controls in airliners.\nVariants offer <a href="/wiki/Maximum_take-off_weight" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximum take-off weight">maximum take-off weights</a> from 68 to 93.5&#160;t (150,000 to 206,000&#160;lb), to cover a 5,740\xe2\x80\x936,940&#160;km (3,100\xe2\x80\x933,750&#160;nmi) <a href="/wiki/Range_(aircraft)" class="mw-redirect" title="Range (aircraft)">range</a>.\nThe 31.4&#160;m (103&#160;ft) long <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A318" title="Airbus A318">A318</a> typically accommodates 107 to 132 passengers.\nThe 124-156 seats <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">A319</a> is 33.8&#160;m (111&#160;ft) long.\nThe A320 is 37.6&#160;m (123&#160;ft) long and can accommodate 150 to 186 passengers.\nThe 44.5&#160;m (146&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">A321</a> offers 185 to 230 seats.\nThe <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jets" title="Airbus Corporate Jets">Airbus Corporate Jets</a> are business jet versions.\n</p><p>In December 2010, Airbus announced the <a href="/wiki/Re-engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Re-engine">re-engined</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo_family" title="Airbus A320neo family">A320neo</a> (<i>new engine option)</i>, which entered service with <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> in January 2016.\nWith more efficient turbofans and improvements including <a href="/wiki/Winglet" class="mw-redirect" title="Winglet">sharklets</a>, it offers up to 15% better <a href="/wiki/Fuel_economy_in_aircraft" title="Fuel economy in aircraft">fuel economy</a>.\nEarlier A320s are now called <b>A320ceo</b> (<i>current engine option</i>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> is the largest A320 operator as of March 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-aamerger_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aamerger-4">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> In October 2019, the A320 family surpassed the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> to become the highest-selling airliner. \nAs of October 2020, a total of 9,572 aircraft had been <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A320_operators" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Airbus A320 operators">delivered</a> to more than 330 operators, with 9,053 aircraft in service. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A320_orders" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Airbus A320 orders">Orders</a> pending were 6,010, for a total of 15,582 orders.\nThe A320ceo initially competed with the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Classic" title="Boeing 737 Classic">737 Classic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-80" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-80">MD-80</a>, then their successors, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">737 Next Generation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-90" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-90">MD-90</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">737 MAX</a> is Boeing\'s response to the A320neo.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Development"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Development</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Origins"><span tocsection-20"><a href="#Engines"><span class="tocnumber">2.4</span> <span class="toctext">Engines</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Competition</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Maintenance"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span
