2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="520" /></a></div></div>\n\t\t\t<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/PW6000" class="mw-redirect" title="PW6000">PW6000</a> is available on the smallest A318\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">Operational history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Operational history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Joint_Aviation_Authorities" title="Joint Aviation Authorities">Joint Aviation Authorities</a> (JAA) issued the <a href="/wiki/Type_certificate" title="Type certificate">type certificate</a> for the A320 on 26 February 1988. After entering the market on 18 April 1988 with Air France, Airbus then expanded the A320 family rapidly, launching the 185-seat A321 in 1989 and first delivered it in 1994; launching the 124-seat A319 in 1993 and delivering it in 1996; and launching the 107-seat A318 in 1999 with first deliveries in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UnitedandVA_32315_(16735062459).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg/220px-UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg/330px-UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg/440px-UnitedandVA_32315_%2816735062459%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1978" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UnitedandVA_32315_(16735062459).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The A320 family (background) main competition is the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737 Next Generation</a> (foreground)</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Competition_between_Airbus_and_Boeing#Airbus_A320_vs_Boeing_737" title="Competition between Airbus and Boeing">Competition between Airbus and Boeing \xc2\xa7&#160;Airbus A320 vs Boeing 737</a></div>\n<p>The A320 family was developed to compete with the Boeing 737 Classics (-300/-400/-500) and the McDonnell Douglas MD-80/90 series, and has since faced challenges from the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737 Next Generation</a> (-600/-700/-800/-900) and the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_717" title="Boeing 717">717</a> during its two decades in service. As of 2010, as well as the 737, the A320 family faces competition from <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Embraer_E-Jets" class="mw-redirect" title="Embraer E-Jets">E-195</a> (to the A318), and the <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_CSeries" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier CSeries">CSeries</a> being developed by <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier</a><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> to the A318/A319.\n</p><p>Airbus has delivered 8,605 A320 family aircraft since their certification/first delivery in early 1988, with another 6,056 on firm order (as of 31 December 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In comparison, Boeing has shipped 10,444 737 series since late 1967, with 8,918<sup id="cite_ref-Historic_Boeing_1988-2018_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Historic_Boeing_1988-2018-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> of those deliveries since March 1988,<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing_O-D_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing_O-D-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and has a further 4,763 on firm order (as of 31 December 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-O_D_737_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O_D_737-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:600px;min-height:200px" data-graph-id="a7a1807e9750532b7cf163e32e9df7938f5e629b"></div>\n<ul><li><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:green; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320_family#Orders_and_deliveries" title="Airbus A320 family">Airbus A320 family deliveries</a><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Hist_OD_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Hist_OD-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_O_D_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_O_D-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></div></li>\n<li><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="background-color:blue; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Boeing_737#Total_production" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737 series deliveries</a><sup id="cite_ref-Boeing_Hist_Deliveries_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing_Hist_Deliveries-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></div></li></ul>\n<dl><dd><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist"><span>This graph: </span><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Navbar" title="Template:Navbar"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Navbar" title="Template talk:Navbar"><span title="Discuss this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div></dd></dl>\n<p>By September 2018, there were 7,251 A320 family ceo aircraft in service versus 6,757 737NGs, while Airbus expected to deliver 3,174 <a href="/wiki/A320neo" class="mw-redirect" title="A320neo">A320neos</a> compared with 2,999 <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX" title="Boeing 737 MAX">Boeing 737 MAX</a> through 2022.\nAirbus sold the A320 well to low-cost startups and offering a choice of engines could make them more attractive to airlines and lessors than the single sourced 737, but CFM engines are extremely reliable.\nThe six-month head-start of the A320neo allowed Airbus to rack up 1,000 orders before Boeing announced the MAX.\nThe A321 has outsold the 737-900 three to one, as the A321neo is again dominating the 737-9 MAX, to be joined by the 737-10 MAX.<sup id="cite_ref-MRO29aug2018_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MRO29aug2018-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance">Maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/A_Check" class="mw-redirect" title="A Check">A Checks</a> are every 750 flight hours and structural inspections are at six- and 12-year intervals.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Replacement_airliner">Replacement airliner</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Replacement airliner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2006, Airbus was studying a future replacement for the A320 series, tentatively dubbed <i><a href="/wiki/Airbus_NSR" title="Airbus NSR">NSR</a></i>, for "New Short-Range aircraft".<sup id="cite_ref-fi_737rs_nsr_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fi_737rs_nsr-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The follow-on aircraft to replace the A320 was named <i>A30X</i>. Airbus North America President Barry Eccleston stated that the earliest the aircraft could have been available was 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In January 2010, <a href="/wiki/John_Leahy_(executive)" title="John Leahy (executive)">John Leahy</a>, Airbus\'s chief operating officer-customers, stated that an all-new single-aisle aircraft was unlikely to be constructed before 2024 or 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Variants">Variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A32XFAMILYv1.0.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A32XFAMILYv1.0.png/220px-A32XFAMILYv1.0.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A32XFAMILYv1.0.png/330px-A32XFAMILYv1.0.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A32XFAMILYv1.0.png/440px-A32XFAMILYv1.0.png 2x" data-file-width="1831" data-file-height="1335" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A32XFAMILYv1.0.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airbus A32X family</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the Airbus A320neo or New Engine Option variants, see <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320neo_family#Variants" title="Airbus A320neo family">Airbus A320neo family \xc2\xa7&#160;Variants</a>.</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The baseline A320 has given rise to a family of aircraft which share a common design but with passenger capacity ranges from 100, on the A318,<sup id="cite_ref-A318_specifications_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A318_specifications-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> to 220, on the A321.<sup id="cite_ref-A321_specifications_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A321_specifications-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> They compete with the 737, 757, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_717" title="Boeing 717">717</a>. Because the four variants share the same flight deck, all have the same pilot <a href="/wiki/Type_rating" title="Type rating">type rating</a>. Today all variants are available as <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jets" title="Airbus Corporate Jets">corporate jets</a>. An A319 variant known as <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319#A319LR" title="Airbus A319">A319LR</a> is also developed. Military versions like <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319_MPA" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319 MPA">A319 MPA</a> also exists. <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> is the largest airline operator of the A320 family of aircraft with 392 aircraft in service as of 30 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Technically, the name "A320" only refers to the original mid-sized aircraft, but it is often informally used to indicate any of the A318/A319/A320/A321 family. All variants are able to be <a href="/wiki/ETOPS" title="ETOPS">ETOPS</a> (Extended-range Twin-engine Operational Performance Standards) certified for 180 minutes since 2004 (<a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">EASA</a>) and 2006 (<a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> With launch of the new Airbus A320neo project, the previous members of the Airbus A320 family received the "current engine option" or "CEO" name.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A320">A320</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: A320">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A320-231,_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg/220px-Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg/330px-Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg/440px-Airbus_A320-231%2C_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A320-231,_Indian_Airlines_AN1471642.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a> A320 with double-<a href="/wiki/Bogie" title="Bogie">bogie</a> main landing gear for lower <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a> loads</div></div></div>\n<p>The A320 series has two variants, the <i>A320-100</i> and <i>A320-200</i>.  Only 21 A320-100s were produced.<sup id="cite_ref-NorrisWagner1999_10-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorrisWagner1999-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> These aircraft, the first to be manufactured, were delivered to <a href="/wiki/Air_Inter" title="Air Inter">Air Inter</a>&#160;&#8211;&#32; later acquired by Air France&#160;&#8211;&#32; and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> as a result of an order from <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> made prior to its acquisition.\n</p><p>The primary changes of the -200 over the -100 are <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device#Wingtip_fence" title="Wingtip device">wingtip fences</a> and increased fuel capacity for increased range. <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines" title="Indian Airlines">Indian Airlines</a> used its first 31 A320-200s with double-<a href="/wiki/Bogie" title="Bogie">bogie</a> main landing gear for airfields with poor runway condition which a single-bogie main gear could not manage.\n</p><p>Powered by two CFM56-5s or IAE V2500s with thrust ratings of 98\xe2\x80\x93120&#160;kN (22,000\xe2\x80\x9327,000&#160;lbf), its typical range with 150 passengers is 3,300 nmi / 6,100&#160;km.<sup id="cite_ref-A320_specifications_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A320_specifications-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A total of 4,512 of the A320ceo model have been delivered, with 220 remaining on order as of 30 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The closest Boeing competitor is the <a href="/wiki/737-800" class="mw-redirect" title="737-800">737-800</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-A320vsB737_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A320vsB737-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1988, the value of a new A320 was $30 million, reaching $40 million by the end of the 1990s, a 30% increase lower than the <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>, it dipped to $37 million after 2001, then peaked to $47 million in 2008, and stabilised at $40\xe2\x80\x9342 million until the transition to the A320neo.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2018, its list price was US$101.0 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_prices_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_prices-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A321">A321</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: A321">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg/220px-Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg/330px-Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg/440px-Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="1182" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A321_-_myAustrian_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The A321 is 6.93&#160;m (22.7&#160;ft) longer; overwing exits are replaced by doors</div></div></div>\n<p>As the A320 began operations in 1988, the A321 was launched as its first derivative.<sup id="cite_ref-NorrisWagner1999_10-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorrisWagner1999-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The A321 fuselage is stretched by 6.93 metres (22&#160;ft 9&#160;in) with a 4.27&#160;m (14&#160;ft 0&#160;in) front plug immediately forward of wing and a 2.67&#160;m (8&#160;ft 9&#160;in) rear plug.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunston_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunston-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The A321-100 maximum takeoff weight is increased by 9,600&#160;kg (21,200&#160;lb) to 83,000&#160;kg (183,000&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-NorrisWagner1999_10-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorrisWagner1999-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> To maintain performance, double-slotted flaps were included, in addition to increasing the wing area by 4&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (43&#160;sq&#160;ft), to 128&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,380&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-A321_described_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A321_described-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The maiden flight of the first of two prototypes came on 11 March 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-Eden_15-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eden-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The A321-100 entered service in January 1994 with Lufthansa.\n</p><p>As the A321-100 range was reduced compared to the A320, the heavier and longer range A321-200 development was launched in 1995. This is achieved through higher thrust engines (V2533-A5 or CFM56-5B3), minor structural strengthening, and an increase in fuel capacity with the installation of one or two optional 2,990&#160;L (790&#160;US&#160;gal) tanks in the rear underfloor hold.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunston_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunston-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Its fuel capacity is increased to 30,030&#160;L (7,930&#160;US&#160;gal) and its maximum takeoff weight to 93,000&#160;kg (205,000&#160;lb). It first flew in December 1996 and entered service with <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a> in April 1997.\n</p><p>Its closest Boeing competitors are the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737NG" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737NG">737-900/900ER</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-A320vsB737_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A320vsB737-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and the 757-200.<sup id="cite_ref-A321_described_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A321_described-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A total of 1,562 of the A321ceo model have been delivered, with 231 remaining on order as of 30 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2018, the A321 list price was US$118.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_prices_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_prices-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A319">A319</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: A319">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319_Austrian_Airlines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 3.73&#160;m (12.2&#160;ft) shorter A319 has a single overwing exit per side for an exit limit of 145, two above<sup id="cite_ref-typecert_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-typecert-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The A319 is 3.73&#160;m (12&#160;ft 3&#160;in) shorter than the A320.<sup id="cite_ref-A320_specifications_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A320_specifications-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meeting_demand_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meeting_demand-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A319_specifications_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A319_specifications-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\nAlso known as the A320M-7, it is a shortened, minimum-change version of the A320 with four frames fore of the wing and three frames aft of the wing removed. With a similar fuel capacity as the A320-200 and fewer passengers, the range with 124 passengers in a two-class configuration extends to 6,650&#160;km (3,590&#160;nmi), or 6,850&#160;km (3,700&#160;nmi) with the "Sharklets".<sup id="cite_ref-A319_specifications_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A319_specifications-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Four propulsion options available on the A319 are the 23,040\xe2\x80\x9324,800&#160;lbf (102.5\xe2\x80\x93110.3&#160;kN) IAE V2500, or the 22,000\xe2\x80\x9327,000&#160;lbf (98\xe2\x80\x93120&#160;kN) CFM56.<sup id="cite_ref-Gunston_7-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gunston-7">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Although identical to those of the A320, these engines are derated because of the A319\'s lower MTOW.\n</p><p>The A319 was developed at the request of <a href="/wiki/Steven_F._Udvar-H%C3%A1zy" title="Steven F. Udvar-H\xc3\xa1zy">Steven F. Udvar-H\xc3\xa1zy</a>, the former president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/ILFC" class="mw-redirect" title="ILFC">ILFC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The A319\'s launch customer, in fact, was ILFC, which had placed an order for six A319s by 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-NorrisWagner1999_10-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorrisWagner1999-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Anticipating further orders by Swissair and Alitalia, Airbus decided to launch the programme on 10 June 1993.  Final assembly of the first A319 began on 23 March 1995<sup id="cite_ref-Eden_15-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eden-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and it was first introduced with Swissair in April 1996. The direct <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> competitor is the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700</a>.\n</p><p>A total of 1,460 of the A319ceo model have been delivered with 24 remaining on order as of 30 September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\nA 1998 A319 value was $35 million new, was halved by 2009, and reached scrap levels by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2018, the A319 list price was US$92.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_prices_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_prices-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ACJ319">ACJ319 <span class="anchor" id="A319LR"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: ACJ319">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_(11423487003).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg/220px-9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg/330px-9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg/440px-9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_%2811423487003%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1063" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:9H-AVK_Airbus_A319-115_CJ_(11423487003).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An ACJ319 cabin</div></div></div>\n<p>The A319CJ (rebranded ACJ319) is the corporate jet version of the A319. It incorporates removable extra fuel tanks (up to six additional center tanks) which are installed in the cargo compartment, and an increased service ceiling of 12,500&#160;m (41,000&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-a319cjceiling_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a319cjceiling-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Range with eight passengers\' payload and auxiliary fuel tanks (ACTs) is up to 11,000 kilometres (6,000&#160;nmi).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Upon resale, the aircraft can be reconfigured as a standard A319 by removing its extra tanks and corporate cabin outfit, thus maximising its resale value. It was formerly also known as the ACJ, or <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Corporate_Jets" title="Airbus Corporate Jets">Airbus Corporate Jet</a>, while starting with 2014 it has the marketing designation ACJ319.\n</p><p>The aircraft seats up to 39 passengers, but may be outfitted by the customers into any configuration. <a href="/wiki/Tyrolean_Jet_Services" title="Tyrolean Jet Services">Tyrolean Jet Services</a> Mfg. GmbH &amp; CO KG, <a href="/wiki/MJET" title="MJET">MJET</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reliance_Industries" title="Reliance Industries">Reliance Industries</a> are among its users. The A319CJ competes with other ultralarge-cabin corporate jets such as the Boeing 737-700-based <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Business_Jet" title="Boeing Business Jet">Boeing Business Jet</a> (BBJ) and <a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> <a href="/wiki/Lineage_1000" class="mw-redirect" title="Lineage 1000">Lineage 1000</a>, as well as with large-cabin and ultralong-range <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_G650" title="Gulfstream G650">Gulfstream G650</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulfstream_G550" title="Gulfstream G550">Gulfstream G550</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Aerospace" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Aerospace">Bombardier</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Global_6000" class="mw-redirect" title="Global 6000">Global 6000</a>. It is powered by the same engine types as the A320. The A319CJ was used by the <i><a href="/wiki/Escadron_de_transport,_d%27entrainement_et_de_calibration" class="mw-redirect" title="Escadron de transport, d&#39;entrainement et de calibration">Escadron de Transport, d\'Entra\xc3\xaenement et de Calibration</a></i> which is in charge of transportation for France\'s officials and also by the Flugbereitschaft of the <a href="/wiki/German_Air_Force" title="German Air Force">German Air Force</a> for transportation of Germany\'s officials. An ACJ serves as a presidential or official aircraft of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A318">A318</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: A318">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A318-112_(19751900080).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg/220px-Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg/330px-Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg/440px-Airbus_A318-112_%2819751900080%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A318-112_(19751900080).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 31.44&#160;m (103.1&#160;ft) long A318 is the shortest variant, here in livery of British Airways.</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A318" title="Airbus A318">Airbus A318</a></div>\n<p>The Airbus A318 is the smallest member of the Airbus A320 family. The A318 carries up to 132 passengers and has a maximum range of 5,700&#160;km (3,100&#160;nmi). The aircraft entered service in July 2003 with Frontier Airlines, and shares a common type rating with all other Airbus A320 family variants, allowing existing A320 family pilots to fly the aircraft without the need for further training. It is the largest commercial aircraft certified by the European Aviation Safety Agency for steep approach operations, allowing flights at airports such as <a href="/wiki/London_City_Airport" title="London City Airport">London City Airport</a>. Relative to other Airbus A320 family variants, the A318 has sold in only small numbers with total orders for only 80 aircraft placed as of 31&#160;October&#160;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.\nIn 2018, the A318 list price was US$77.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_prices_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_prices-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freighter_conversion">Freighter conversion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Freighter conversion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TC-OBJ_(22903366601).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg/220px-TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg/330px-TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg/440px-TC-OBJ_%2822903366601%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TC-OBJ_(22903366601).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MSN 835, the first converted A321, in passenger form</div></div></div>\n<p>A programme to convert A320 and A321 aircraft into <a href="/wiki/Cargo_aircraft" title="Cargo aircraft">freighters</a> was set up by Airbus Freighter Conversion GmbH. Airframes would be converted by <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Flugzeugwerke" title="Elbe Flugzeugwerke">Elbe Flugzeugwerke</a> <a href="/wiki/GmbH" class="mw-redirect" title="GmbH">GmbH</a> (EFW) in <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, Germany, and <a href="/wiki/Zhukovsky_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zhukovsky (city)">Zhukovsky</a>, Russia. The launch customer <a href="/wiki/Cerberus_Capital_Management" title="Cerberus Capital Management">AerCap</a> signed a firm contract on 16 July 2008 to convert 30 of AerCap\'s passenger A320/A321s into A320/A321P2F (passenger to freighter). However, on 3 June 2011, Airbus announced all partners would end the passenger to freighter programme, citing high demand for used airframes for passenger service.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 June 2015 <a href="/wiki/ST_Aerospace" title="ST Aerospace">ST Aerospace</a> signed agreements with Airbus and EFW for a collaboration to launch the A320/A321 passenger-to-freighter (P2F) conversion programme.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\nIn August 2019, <a href="/wiki/Qantas_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Qantas Airways">Qantas Airways</a> was announced as the launch operator for the A321P2F converted freighter, for <a href="/wiki/Australia_Post" title="Australia Post">Australia Post</a>, with up to three aircraft to be introduced in October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Titan Airways received their first A321P2F in January 2021<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> which was converted at Singapore Seletar Airport, the airline has two more A321P2F\'s that are yet to be converted.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The initial converted aircraft first flew on 22 January 2020, to be delivered to Vallair, and it secured EASA <a href="/wiki/Supplementary_type_certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Supplementary type certificate">supplementary type certificate</a> in February.\nIt should replace older converted Boeing 757s with 14 positions on the main deck and 10 on the lower, lifting up to 27.9&#160;t (62,000&#160;lb) over 4,300&#160;km (2,300&#160;nmi).\nAirbus sees a market for 1,000 narrowbody conversions over the 2020-2040 period.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight25feb2020_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight25feb2020-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> On 27 October 2020, the first A321P2F was delivered to launch operator Qantas Airways, with windows and exit doors removed, and a large hydraulically actuated main cargo door installed.<sup id="cite_ref-AWM-P2F_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AWM-P2F-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airborne_Early_Warning_conversion">Airborne Early Warning conversion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airborne Early Warning conversion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(India)" title="Ministry of Defence (India)">Indian Defence Ministry</a> greenlit the modification by the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Research_and_Development_Organisation" title="Defence Research and Development Organisation">Defence Research and Development Organisation</a> of six <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a> A320s into <a href="/wiki/Airborne_early_warning_and_control" title="Airborne early warning and control">Airborne early warning and control</a> planes for Rs 10,5000 <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">crore</a> (US$149 million). They are to complement the two Indian-built <a href="/wiki/DRDO_AEW%26CS" title="DRDO AEW&amp;CS">Netra</a> and three Israeli-Russian-made <a href="/wiki/EL/M-2075" title="EL/M-2075">PHALCON</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Operators">Operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Operators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_(N657AW,_N837AW,_N604AW,_N845NN)_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg/220px-American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg/330px-American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg/440px-American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_%28N657AW%2C_N837AW%2C_N604AW%2C_N845NN%29_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6240" data-file-height="4160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:American_Airlines_aircraft_at_PHX_(N657AW,_N837AW,_N604AW,_N845NN)_-_Quintin_Soloviev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> is the largest A320 operator</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A320_family_operators" title="List of Airbus A320 family operators">List of Airbus A320 family operators</a></div>\n<p>As of March&#160;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were 9,247 A320 family aircraft in commercial service with over 330 operators. It includes 65 A318, 1,398 A319 (1,395 ceo + 3 neo), 5,553 A320 (4,349 ceo + 1,204 neo) and 2,231 A321 (1,725 ceo + 506 neo) aircraft. All 1,713 delivered A320neo family aircraft were in service, while 543 A320ceo family aircraft consisting of 15 A318, 88 A319, 403 A320 and 45 A321 were out of service through retirement or write-off. The five largest operators were American Airlines operating 430, <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a> 345, EasyJet 336, China Southern Airlines 309 and <a href="/wiki/IndiGo" title="IndiGo">IndiGo</a> 268 airplanes.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\nAir France and British Airways have been the only operators to operate all four variants of the A320ceo family.<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> received the milestone airplane, an A320ceo with the manufacturer serial number (MSN) 5,000, on 20 January 2012<sup id="cite_ref-MSN5TSD_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSN5TSD-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and eight years later the MSN 10,000, an A321neo, at the celebration of its 75th anniversary on 9 October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-MSN10TSD_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSN10TSD-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MSN10TSD2_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSN10TSD2-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orders_and_deliveries">Orders and deliveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Orders and deliveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A320_orders" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Airbus A320 orders">List of Airbus A320 orders</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Airbus_A320neo_family_orders_and_deliveries" title="List of Airbus A320neo family orders and deliveries">List of Airbus A320neo family orders and deliveries</a></div>\n<p>The A320ceo family ranked as the world\'s fastest-selling airliner according to records from 2005 to 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The record was then improved by the successor, the A320neo family, with 1,420 orders and commitments in less than a year during the <a href="/wiki/Dubai_Airshow" title="Dubai Airshow">Dubai Airshow</a> in November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of October 2019, the A320 family backlog stood at over 6,000 again, including 78 remaining A320ceos, bringing the total orders to 15,193, surpassing the Boeing 737\'s total of 15,136 and making the A320 family the world\'s highest-selling airliner. In terms of deliveries, 9,086 A320 family aircraft had been delivered since 1988, nearly 1,500 fewer than the 10,563 of the 737 series delivered since 1967, around 21 years earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight15nov2019_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight15nov2019-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of March&#160;2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, a total of 9,798 A320 family aircraft had been delivered with 42 A320ceos (3 A319s, 18 A320s and 21 A321s) to be delivered. Airbus delivered 9 A320ceo variants over the first three months of 2021 compared to 96 A320neo variants. The A320 family backlog was below the 6,000 mark and total orders reached 15,499,<sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> whereas cancellations incurred during the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_MAX_groundings" title="Boeing 737 MAX groundings">Boeing 737 MAX groundings</a> brought total orders for the 737 down to 14,690 of which 10,677 aircraft had been delivered.<sup id="cite_ref-Boeing_O-D_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boeing_O-D-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" A320neo --\n</th>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-</td>\n<td>-\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>(A320 family)\n</th>\n<td><b>(491)</b></td>\n<td><b>(490)</b></td>\n<td><b>(493)</b></td>\n<td><b>(455)</b></td>\n<td><b>(421)</b></td>\n<td><b>(401)</b></td>\n<td><b>(402)</b></td>\n<td><b>(386)</b></td>\n<td><b>(367)</b></td>\n<td><b>(339)</b></td>\n<td><b>(289)</b></td>\n<td><b>(233)</b></td>\n<td><b>(233)</b></td>\n<td><b>(236)</b></td>\n<td><b>(257)</b></td>\n<td><b>(241)</b></td>\n<td><b>(222)</b></td>\n<td><b>(168)</b></td>\n<td><b>(127)</b></td>\n<td><b>(72)</b></td>\n<td><b>(56)</b></td>\n<td><b>(64)</b></td>\n<td><b>(71)</b></td>\n<td><b>(111)</b></td>\n<td><b>(119)</b></td>\n<td><b>(58)</b></td>\n<td><b>(58)</b></td>\n<td><b>(16)</b>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b><small><i>Data through end of March 2021.</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Orders_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Orders-5">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Airbus_Hist_OD_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airbus_Hist_OD-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup></b>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accidents_and_incidents_involving_the_Airbus_A320_family" title="List of accidents and incidents involving the Airbus A320 family">List of accidents and incidents involving the Airbus A320 family</a></div>\n<p>For the entire A320 family, 159 major <a href="/wiki/Aviation_accidents_and_incidents" title="Aviation accidents and incidents">aviation accidents and incidents</a> have occurred,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> including 47 <a href="/wiki/Hull_loss" title="Hull loss">hull loss</a> accidents (latest one being <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines_Flight_8303" title="Pakistan International Airlines Flight 8303">Pakistan International Airlines Flight 8303</a> on 22 May 2020),<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and a total of 1393 fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 June 1988, <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_296" title="Air France Flight 296">Air France Flight 296</a> crashed into trees at the end of runway at <a href="/wiki/Mulhouse-Habsheim_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mulhouse-Habsheim Airport">Mulhouse-Habsheim Airport</a>, three out of 130 passengers were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In February 1990 another A320, <a href="/wiki/Indian_Airlines_Flight_605" title="Indian Airlines Flight 605">Indian Airlines Flight 605</a>, crash-landed short of the airport runway in <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bangalore</a>, the ensuing fire contributed to the casualty count of 92 of 146 on board.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The press and media later questioned the fly-by-wire flight control system, but subsequent investigations by commission of inquiry found "no malfunction of the aircraft or its equipment which could have contributed towards a reduction in safety or an increase in the crew\'s workload during the final flight phase&#160;... the response of the engines was normal and in compliance with certification requirement."<sup id="cite_ref-Reed_p.84_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reed_p.84-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It has seen 50 incidents where several flight displays were lost.<sup id="cite_ref-NTSB_safety_recommendation_A08-53_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NTSB_safety_recommendation_A08-53-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Through 2015, the Airbus A320 family has experienced 0.12 fatal hull-loss accidents for every million takeoffs and 0.26 total hull-loss accidents for every million takeoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Specifications">Specifications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Airbus_A320_family&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Specifications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table
